More neutral and a wider sound stage. Sony's default frequency response is very very bass heavy to the point it actually sounds muddy. Apple also has slightly better NC, better transperency mode and waaaayyyy better call quality. Not to mention that Apple's encoding for AAC is better than Android or Windows. Apple can do wonders with 320kbps AAC audio just because of how excellent and optimized their encoding/decoding is. 

But again, the price of the headphones, their shoddy support for non-Apple devices and the fact that they don't come with any decent carrying case is why they are a bad value.

[230] âœ… @RaymondwLin  ğŸ‘2  2024-12-02
åŸæ–‡ï¼šI just finally upgraded from the XM1 to these XM4....In my brief time, here are the main differences.

1 - The case for the XM1 is nicer. Strap on the case is nicer, it feels more study, the faux leather is nicer than the linen on the XM4.
2 - The XM1 is better built, more metal parts. The faux leather texture on the outside of the ear cup is nicer than rubberised texture on the XM4.
3 - The XM1's strap has 10 clicks, the XM4 has 9.  XM1 can fits larger heads.
4 - XM1's headband's angle is wider, it is a more comfortable pair to wear.
5 - XM1 sounds more open, better clarity.
6 - ANC on XM4 is better.

USB-C on the XM4 is basically why I upgraded, but besides the ANC and some tech features.  XM1 is better in almost every other way.  Better materials, better sounding, better built, better case.

[285] âŒ @df446  ğŸ‘0  2024-09-19
åŸæ–‡ï¼šI found these subpar, and returned them after 18 hours.  Major problems: the noise cancellation pauses at random.  Not as the results of speaking or any other sound that may trigger the SPEAK-TO-CHAT, but the problem seems to be correlated with picking up the device that's playing the tracks, and or using the Next Track function on the playing device.  I didn't have time to test it - that was Sony's job.  The "buttons".  The buttons to activate functions like Next/Previous Track, Volume Up/Down, etc, are simply touch pads on the right earpiece.   The problem is there's no map on the earpiece indicating where the "touch" zone might be for any particular function, so one ends up hunting around with one's finger.  This results in erroneous commands such as Next Track, when one actually meant Volume Up, or Pause, for example.  Simply embossing something small onto the zones where the controls are (little dots, for example) would give one's fingers something to map the individual functions by.

    æƒ…æ„Ÿï¼šnegative (ç½®ä¿¡åº¦ 0.82)

    â†³  @richardw1992  ğŸ‘5  2020-08-13
    åŸæ–‡ï¼š@EpicFailcze I'm glad you asked, I spent several weeks auditioning about 15+ different headsets before deciding which to get. 

The best sounding Bluetooth ANC headphones I've tried are without a doubt the Master & Dynamic MW65, their frequency response is phenomenal (only when they're in wireless mode), but their ANC isn't very good and the passive seal of the ear cups isn't very good. So they're actually not much good for the situations you would probably want them, i.e. commuting or on the go. On sound quality alone though these really moved me.

The second best sounding I've auditioned is the Jabra Elite 85H. These are also fantastic all rounders, comfy, great ANC and microphone quality, and great value. IMO the sound quality of the Jabras puts the competition from Bose, Sony, Sennheiser, B&W, B&O (you name it...) to shame.

A lot of consumer headphones tend to have an over emphasised bass response (the Sony XM3s are a prime example of this). On first listen this sounds appealing and the average consumer will normally be quite satisfied. It you take the time to compare different headphoned side by side you will notice there is a lot more to a good balanced sound than just having strong bass. To much bass will mask and cover up detail in mid range instruments such as piano, guitar, vocals etc. A lack of treble or a quiet treble in comparison to the bass level will make them sound less detailed and have less clarity. It's important for the midrange to be smooth and consistent too without any dips or peaks so that instruments appear at the right levels and position in the mix. 

The Jabras Impressed me because the bass was strong and tight without any unnecessary boom and bloat. They had a prominent and smooth midrange, whereas a lot of consumer headphones are V-shaped or scooped out, and the treble was also nice and detailed without sounding harsh.

There used to be a great YouTube reviewer called Jim's Review Rooms where he did sound comparisons. Whilst this in noway compared to listening to them in the flesh it's a great way to start to understand how much the sound can change from one headset to another.

The most disappointing headsets I listened to in the wireless ANC bracket were the Sony XM3s, the B&W PX7s and the Sennheiser Momentum wireless 3s. 

Top 3 in order would be the M&D MW65, Jabra Elite 85h and 3rd place would probably be the Bose 700. Having grown to dislike most of Bose' offerings the 700s are actually a remarkably balanced set of headphones, they smooth out some of the midrange problems that the QC35 have and generally sound good.

Now part of my views will all be down to taste. I mainly listen to a lot of bass heavy electronic music such as tech and house, so this is partly why the bass heavy headphones sound so bad to me, because it's just overpowering. However, when I listen to rock/metal which has much less bass in the mixing/mastering of the music the headphones which sounded so horrible to me with house music do start to give the music a bit more life and ooomph in the lower frequencies. In fact metal thrived of thick low mids and the Sony's compliment that quite well, to some extent. This doesn't make up for their general lack of detail and muddiness however.

My advice, buy the Jabras, you won't regret it.

    â†³ âŒ @qps9380  ğŸ‘1  2020-08-13

    â†³  @richardw1992  ğŸ‘0  2020-08-13
    åŸæ–‡ï¼š@qps9380 yes I used all the companion apps and had a play with the equalisers to see how they reacted, my general focus was however on comparing them all flat without DSP to make it a fair playing field. 

Whilst in theory you could apply such drastic DSP/EQ through software to completely alter the sound of a headset, this would only be attempting to cover up for that headsets lack of ability to perform correctly out of the box. DSP is very powerful, but there is a lot of analogue engineering that goes into fine tuning sound from the materials used in the speaker diaphragm, the magnet type, the size of the ear cups and chamber, the material of the ear pads etc. Interestingly one headphone I tried had such drastic factory DSP applied which you were unable to turn off, it initially sounded fantastically flat and transparent then I quickly realised there was compression on certain transients where the software couldn't keep up with the music it and it ended up all over the place! They were called the "Cleer Flow II" a prime example of how DSP alone can't polish a turd. 

Furthermore, the companion app would only apply to my phone. So if I wanted to listen to music on a laptop for example then those EQ / DSP tweaks wouldn't be present. I've also heard on the Sony's that if you use an advanced codec like LDAC or aptX the equaliser is disabled?

[520]  @charlescain4231  ğŸ‘3  2022-04-17
åŸæ–‡ï¼šI owned these a few months ago and now I have some thoughts. 
I thought these were amazing when I first bought them, couldn't believe how good they sounded. Even in those early days though, sometimes I thought "jee I just wish it was slightly clearer" but because I spent so much on them I just assumed this is about as good as it got and just got used to it.
Then however I found a great youtuber called crinacle and he kinda slagged on them a bit, basically calling them beats and that's when it all started falling apart, what I'd be slightly feelng previous was now perfectly crystalised and it's issues of the bass basically bleeding all the way into the mids was unavoidable for me. So I went out and bought a second hand pair of Beyerdynamic DT 990s and instantly the difference was night and day, the DT 990s just were so much clearer with much more detail and were frankly much better tuned. This was just running out of my phone too, no amp or dac yet (which you can do even though they are the 250ohm version). It got to the point where it dawned on me that I'll never use the sonys again so I sold them and haven't looked back since.
 Now this is all to say that they weren't what I was looking for, I was chasing sound quality not a feature rich HEADSET. Most of the features are ones I can live without but that will be on a person to person basis

    â†³  @PirtDotato  ğŸ‘9  2020-08-14
    åŸæ–‡ï¼š@00O3O1B Dude wait. Think like a normal person

It's a noise cancelling and Bluetooth headphone but I'm asking how good the sound is like if compared to the Bose 700s
And also about what you have misunderstood.
1. Sound quality refers to how clear and accurate the music is (for average people not someone who expects every byte of data to travel through Bluetooth)
2. The music that we listen to or stream online isn't loseless ever (because the formats are always compressed) so the sound quality is always regarding how accurate the sound is without making some tones flat or too shrill...... In your words if listening to garbage music how accurate and clear the sound of the garbage music is.
3. (Active)Noise cancellation does produce a negative wave to cancel out surrounding noise. And it might sometimes interfere with music to an extent that it's perceptible to human ear. And if active noise cancellation was really bad that it disrupted the original music then people wouldn't want it any way, it would be like listening to a pilot's radio in a sound proof cabin. 
4. Lossless audio requires lot of space and people generally use mp3 or something like that instead of lossless FLACs
5. Sony uses mp3 and other compressed audio formats and fills in the gaps to make it sound like lossless and although it doesn't meet the standards as good as studio monitors do but is quite good for a Bluetooth headphone that uses mp3 instead of lossless as the source.
6. Most importantly sound quality when people ask for is about how clear and rich the sound is if u know what I mean. Like Bose has an in built equalizer that automatically adjusts the audio for a rich experience and if u ask people then obviously Bose has better sound quality than Sony (not technical sound quality but the overall music experience they get).
7. The channel doesn't describe about the audio is how bass heavy or clear, etc.(agreed)... But when people want to know about the sound quality then they DON'T  ask if these can produce highest quality sound without missing the data, rather how good they sound against their competitors like the Bose 700...
It was a totally different question for your answer.

    â†³  @sacken  ğŸ‘17  2020-09-20
    åŸæ–‡ï¼š@fate-vs-destiny8239 In general there are some people that just can't use ANC bc it makes them dizzy, gives'em headache and they can't do really anything about it but the vast majority of people has no problem. Anyway the ANC in these headphones is not really THAT good like those "simulatons" on yt show. The sound isn't just 100% gone. ANC is good at blocking sounds of freqeuncies up to 1kHz. Above that it mostly relies on passive noise cancelation of the headphone themselves. Can't say that these Sony's don't block higher freqeuncies because passive cancelation is good itself and ANC is still  canceling sound just not as good as >1kHz. For example if you stand near the  pretty busy road and listen to a song at reasonable sound level you shouldn't hear any noise, it will be gone, without any music, well the sound will be canceled by idk 80% BUT lets say you are at home listening to music at 50% volume (for me thats high enough, anything above 80% is just pain) and your alarm goes on, you will have no problem hearing that. How about the voices? No music or movie and someone stands near you - you will hear them but understanding what they say might be hard, if you turn on the music or a movie, they are gone. For me, these headphones were the best thing I bought in the last 2 years, even though ANC might be just not as good as they say (its still amazing).

    â†³ âœ… @leander1859  ğŸ‘0  2022-02-07
    åŸæ–‡ï¼šThese use high quality codecs like AAC. Which is very nice on Apple phones, not so much on Android. Since you have a Samsung the older XM3 would have probably better for you, those support aptX and generally give better sound quality on Android devices. Bit disappointing he doesn't mention this in his review.
    æƒ…æ„Ÿï¼špositive (ç½®ä¿¡åº¦ 0.61)

    â†³ âŒ @jame5game5  ğŸ‘0  2022-02-07
    åŸæ–‡ï¼š@leander1859 Really ? So how do I know if an Android phone has good codec ?
    æƒ…æ„Ÿï¼šnegative (ç½®ä¿¡åº¦ 0.59)

    â†³ âœ… @leander1859  ğŸ‘0  2022-02-07
    åŸæ–‡ï¼š@jame5game5 I believe almost all Android phones have aptX nowadays. It's an audio Bluetooth codec to deliver the same sound quality you'd expect from wired headphones. When you buy a bluetooth headphone it's important to look for compatibility. So for the best sound quality on an Android you'd generally want to look for a headset that supports aptX, for Apple that's AAC. Now there is also aptX HD and aptX Adaptive which are the better versions of aptX. I know Samsungs have their own codec. So they don't support aptX HD/Adaptive, only aptX. But most other newer Androids do have the HD/Adaptive codecs. Like Pixel, OnePlus, Xiaomi, Sony, Motorola, LG, Nokia etc. Long story haha but if you're not sure I'd recommend to just google around a bit.
    æƒ…æ„Ÿï¼špositive (ç½®ä¿¡åº¦ 0.50)

    â†³ â– @leander1859  ğŸ‘0  2022-02-07
    åŸæ–‡ï¼š@jame5game5 Usually when you pair your headphone it automatically chooses the best codec. But you can check the codec options (while paired) in your developer settings, under Bluetooth audio codec.
    æƒ…æ„Ÿï¼šneutral (ç½®ä¿¡åº¦ 0.78)

    â†³ âœ… @jame5game5  ğŸ‘1  2022-02-08

åŸæ–‡ï¼šBIG COMPARISON (New and old ones): * Panasonic Technics A800 (owner) vs * Sony MX4 (tested 7 days) vs * Bose QC45 (owner) vs * Panasonic RB-M700BE (owner 5x) vs * Sony MDR-XB950 (Ex-Owner) vs * Sony WHXB910N (tested) : Every headphone has its weaknesses and its strengths :

The Panasonic Technics A800 has very good sound and ANC and it's general volume and bass volume is much stronger and powerfull compared to Sony MX4 or Bose QC45. MX4 and QC45 are pretty the same in sound and ANC. QC45 has better software than MX4. The A800 software is in the level of QC45. The ANC of the Panasonic Technics A800 is much better than on Bose QC45 (And a lot of people say the QC45 has a little bit better ANC than MX4, so that means A800 has to be the best ANC on market at the moment) only exeption heavy vibrations from steps or public transportation... The Panasonic (A800 & RB-M700B) ANC has problems with that... 

The ANC of the RB-M700B is worse but not that much worse than the others. When ANC is deactivated the RB-M700B has the best overall sound imo ! The RB-M700B is the only one you think you have a subwoofer ! That's because it has a spring vibration system (bass reaktor). To listen my favorite music (genre electronic music and techno) and war games with a lot of bassy explosions I prefer to use the Panasonic RB-M700B. I really love the bass reactor vibration system very very very much !!!! It is the only one that feels like you have a 2.1 subwoofer hifi system. On the others new on market you thnink you have a bass weak 2.0 system. Also the mids and highs are good. I have a total of 5x RB-700's (3x from warehouse 75-85â‚¬) to be sure i got great music hp for next 10 years. (Iâ€™m engineer i can replace batteries if storage at optimal voltage is not much enough). Because I live at to places I want minimum 4 head phones (you always need 2 when one is discharged take to otherâ€¦ permanent changeâ€¦). So this matches nicely. I hope Panasonic will continue to offer and develop headphones with bass reactor vibration system because I can't listen to techno and electronic music on head phones without a bass reactor anymore. The Sony MDR-XB950N1 Extra Bass head phones from 2017 have a bass reactor vibration system (my first head phones i had with a bass vibration system) but the new Sony WHXB910N Extra Bass from 2021 don't has a bass vibration system anymore imo. 

I use public transportation and have a very very very permanent noisy neighbor that is the reason I needed something more than the RB-M700B. I use the Bose QC45 for public transportation and the Panasonic Technics A800 for watching TV or silent video games at home when the neighbour is very loud (the A800 can better reduce noises from neighboor than the QC 45, bassy step noises and others).

    åŸæ–‡ï¼š@Ghost-jy9hk So, the overall experience is awesome. But since these are my first ANC headphones, I'd not be able to rate them against their competitors. I'm going to try and explain my experience to you based on the following aspects which are the most fundamental ones:
1. Build quality and design -  Absolutely fantastic. They feel premium and are very minimal. Black ones look sick, trust me. You could stare at 'em all day.

2. Sound quality - The fact that MKBHD doesn't even have to talk about the sound quality speaks volumes. They sound incredible. The sound stage is incredible. You will be able to feel the thumping of those Travis Scott songs' beats. But don't disappoint yourself by listening to a lot of Spotify on these headphones. The songs on Spotify are not high quality audio files. Try and download your music to enjoy these. 

3. Active Noise Cancellation - I haven't been able to put ANC to its true test since I've been using them indoors. I haven't been able to use them outside just yet. But ANC does what it says. Cancels out all the white noise. Only ANC on -- you could hear people talk but the sound will be extremely muffled. ANC on + Music on -- you won't hear a thing.

I love 'em. I think you won't regret buying them. But that would also depend on how much you get them for. 

Hope this helps.
